тАШ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред ‘рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗрд░рд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ тАШ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╣тАЭ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╣рд┐рд╣рд╢рдмреНрджрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рддреНред рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рджреНрдпреЛрд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛ рддрддрдГ рдкрд░рдВ рдирд╡рд░реНрдЪреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╕реНрддрддрдГ рдкрд░рд╛ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрд╛ рддрддрд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рд░реЛрджрд╕реНрдпреЛрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢реА рджреНрдпреБрдирд┐рд╢реЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реА рджрд┐рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрд╛ рддрддрдГ рд╖рдбрд╝реГрдЪреЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рджрдЧреНрдиреЗрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрд╢реНрдЪреЗрддрд┐ рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее

+Jamison Brereton

55 (289)
All Gods
Praj─Бpati Vai┼Ыv─Бmitra or Praj─Бpati V─Бcya
22 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The most obvious feature of this hymn is the refrain found in every verse: тАЬgreat is the one and only lordship of the gods,тАЭ notable for its emphasis on unity (├йkam тАЬone and onlyтАЭ is the final word of each verse) and for the juxtaposition and implied identity of asura(tv├бm) тАЬlord(ship)тАЭ and dev─Б╠Бn─Бm тАЬgods,тАЭ given that in later Vedic the Asuras and the Devas are locked in eternal enmity. This familiar Vedic mystery of simultaneous unity and diversity is further exempli
fied by the references to numerous gods (generally unnamed, but usually recog nizable), especially in the second part of the hymn, in the manner of many All God hymns.
However, the hymn has a more structured trajectory than most All God list hymns. The first part of the hymn treats the mystery of the birth of Agni; once Agni has been definitively born, Indra comes to the sacrifice as is usual. After three verses situating the action at a re-creation of the primordial early-morning sacrifice and introducing the poet (vss. 1тАУ3), the hymn turns to a mystical description of fire dispersed in many places and hidden in the plants (4тАУ5), and of its parents, the two kindling sticks (4тАУ7), then of fire as it catches after the kindling (8тАУ9) and sends its smoke and flames toward heaven (9тАУ10). The kin dling of Agni then takes on both a cosmic and a ritual dimension, as Night and Dawn and then the Dawns alone are identified as the mother(s) of the infant Agni, reflecting, of course, the kindling of the ritual fire at daybreak (11тАУ16). Soon after (17тАУ18) Indra puts in an appearance, coming to the early-morning sacrifice.
Not all the referents are clear in these riddling verses, and in some verses several referents probably lurk beneath the enigmatic phraseology. For example, verse 17 serves as a transition verse between the fire-kindling verses and the appearance of Indra. The bull here could be Agni himself, or Soma (much of the vocabulary is544 III.55
somian), or a prefiguring of Indra. Commentators differ in their identifications, and those given in brackets here are sometimes provisional.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods As noted in the published introduction, this hymn is notable for its refrain, тАЬgreat is the one and only lordship of the godsтАЭ (mah├бd dev─Б╠Бn─Бm asuratv├бm ├йkam), with its juxtaposition of dev├б- and ├бsura-.

рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЙрджрдпрдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрдирд╛рдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╡реНрдпреВрд╖реБрдГ рд╡реНрдпреБрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЕрдз рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЕрдХреНрд╖рд░рдореН ред рди рдХреНрд╖рд░рддреАрддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рдореН ред рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рдорд╣рддреН рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рдЧреЛрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкрджреЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░реЗ рдирднрд╕рд┐ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдереЛрджрд┐рддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рднреВрд╖рдиреН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рд┐рддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╡реНрд░рддрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН рдЙрдк рд╕рдореАрдкрдВ рдиреЗрд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ ред рддрджрд┐рджрдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдПрдХрдВ рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдореН рдЕрд╕реБрд░рддреНрд╡рдореНред рдЕрд╕реНрдпрддрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реБрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рдмрд▓рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рд╡реЛрд╜рд╕реБрд░рддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдмрд▓реНрдпрдореН ред рдорд╣рджреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН рее рд╡реНрдпреВрд╖реБрдГ ред ‘рдЙрд╖ рдкреНрд▓реБрд╖ рджрд╛рд╣реЗ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд▓рд┐рдЯреНрдпреБрд╕рд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред ‘рд╕рд╣’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдпреЛрдЧрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рддреН рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡реГрддреНрддрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рджрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рднреВрд╖рдиреН ред рднрд╡рддреЗрдГ рд╕рдирд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдп рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рддрджрдиреНрддрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрддрд░рд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рдГ ред рд╢рддреБрд░реНрд▓рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдзрд╛рддреБрдХрд╕реНрд╡рд░реЗ рдзрд╛рддреБрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the preceding dawns appear, the great imperishable (light) is engendered in the (firmament, the) sphere of the waters, and then the worshipper is alert to perform the rites (due to) the gods, for great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mahad dev─Бn─Бm asuratvam ekam: this is the burden of this and following verses; asuratvam is the abstract form of asura, explained strong, powerful, prabal─Б, from asyati, who or what throws or impels all things or beings, asyati, ┼Ыipati sarvan: the abstract ispr─Бbalyam or ai┼Ыvaryam, might or sovereigny;

Ekam = one, is explained mukhyam, chief

+Jamison Brereton

Then when the ancient dawns dawned forth, in the track of the cow a great imperishable (syllable) was born [/was discerned],
which tends to the commandments of the gods: great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The perfect in b, v├н jaj├▒e, is entirely ambiguous between тИЪjan and тИЪj├▒─Б, and I think it likely that both are meant. In this context there is not too much difference between a syllable being born and being discerned. The тАЬtrack of the cowтАЭ is presumably here the ritual ground, and the reference is to the ritual speech of the dawn sacrifice. Renou astutely notes the juxtaposition of akс╣г├бra- and pad├б-, reinforcing the speech theme, even though pad├б- has the sense of тАШtrack, footprintтАЩ here. See pad├бin the next vs. (2b) for a possible reference to speech.

The standard tr. all supply a first-person subject in c, with a verb like тАЬI proclaim.тАЭ No one but Oldenberg attempts to justify this addition, and his attempt is halfhearted. I instead take c as continuing b and take the underlying form of prabh┼л╠Бс╣гan to be prabh┼л╠Бс╣гat, neut. nom./acc. sg., before a following nasal, against the Pp. The participle modifies akс╣г├бram in b. In my interpr. the тАЬsyllableтАЭ (that is, the essence of speech) attends to the godsтАЩ commandments, perhaps by giving them imperishable verbal form. I also suggest that the тАЬgreat syllableтАЭ is actually the refrain found in d; note that mah─Б╠Бt in b takes the same position as it does in the refrain. The refrain may also be the most important of the godsтАЩ vratas; see also 6c.

AT the first shining of the earliest Mornings, in the Cow’s home was born the Great Eternal.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet not the gods, Agni, now do us harm, nor the ancient progenitors, who have come to know the degree (of divinity); nor the manifester of light between the two ancient dwellings (earth and heaven, the sun); for great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let not the gods deflect us here, nor the ancient Fathers who know the track [/word], o Agni.
Between the two seats of the two age-old ones [=Heaven and Earth] is your beacon. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

For juhuranta see comm. ad I.43.8; I take the form to тИЪhvс╣Ы тАШgo crookedlyтАЩ, not тИЪhс╣Ы тАШanger, be angryтАЩ. The point here is that the gods and the ancestors, who themselves know the path/word, should not keep us from following this same ritual cursus. There is no question of anger that I can see.

The standard interpr., that c refers to the beacon of the kindled ritual fire visible between heaven and earth, is surely correct. This kindled fire is referred to more straightforwardly in the next vs., 3c s├бmiddhe agna├║.

Let not the Gods here injure us, O Agni, nor Fathers of old time who know the region,
Nor the sign set between two ancient dwellings. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬVariously do my manifold desires alight; present at the solemnity, I recite ancient (hymns); when the fire is kindled we speak indeed the truth, for great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

My desires fly apart in many directions, but with my (ritual) labor I illuminate ancient things.
When Agni has been kindled might we speak only truth: тАЬGreat is the one and only lordship of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The flying, scattered desires of the poet here and his turn, in a ritual context, to the old ways of doing things reminds us of the opening of III.38, a hymn about the development of a poetic vocation within the age-old tradition, esp. III.38.1cd. In this connection itтАЩs worth noting that our refrain, mah├бd dev─Б╠Бn─Бm asuratv├бm ├йkam, finds an echo in III.38.4c mah├бt t├бd vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зo ├бsurasya n─Б╠Бma тАЬGreat is that name of the bull, the lord.тАЭ Geldner also appositely adduces VI.9.6, also about a poetтАЩs training and his selfconscious assumption of the mantle of tradition, with his inspiration deriving from the ritual fire.

The с╣Ыt├б- that we wish to speak may again be the refrain that follows immediately.

+Griffith

My wishes fly abroad to many places: I glance back to the ancient sacrifices.
Let us declare the truth when fire is kindled. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Meine W├╝nsche fliegen nach vielen Seiten, mit rechtem Flei├Я beleuchte ich die fr├╝heren Dinge. Bei dem entflammten Feuer wollen wir die Wahrheit verk├╝nden. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Nach vielen Seiten fliegen meine W├╝nsche, beim Opfer acht’ ich auf die alten Spr├╝che; Bei Agni’s Flamme m├╢gen recht wir preisen; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe universal sovereign is conveyed to many directions; he sleeps in the plural ces of repose; he is connected with the forests; one mother (heaven) nourishes the child; the other (earth) gives him a dwelling; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The universal sovereign: sam─Бn─Б r─Бja may imply either Agni or the Soma

+Jamison Brereton

The common king has been dispersed in many places; he lies in his resting places [=hearths], (spread out) for some distance along the
(fire-)logs.
Another bears the calf; the mother rests peacefully [=the two
fire-churning sticks]. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of
the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The v├н тАж purutr─Б╠Бof the preceding vs. (3a) returns here, though with the preverb bound to a ppl. (v├нbhс╣Ыtaс╕е); the phrase is contrasted with sam─Бn├б- to express the theme of unity and diversity in balance. The тАЬcommon kingтАЭ is of course Agni, and the image is both of this single god being found on many different ritual grounds and of the ritual fire on any particular ritual ground being divided into three.

With Geldner, I assume that the pair in c is the kindling sticks. Cf. III.31.2d and X.27.14b, esp. tastha├║ m─Бt─Б╠БтАЬthe mother stands still,тАЭ comparable to our kс╣г├йti m─Бt─Б╠Б тАЬthe mother rests peacefully.тАЭ The epithet тАШhaving two mothersтАЩ (dvim─Бt├бr-) used of Agni in 6a and 7a is a reference to the paired kindling sticks.

+Griffith

King Universal, born to sundry quarters, extended through the wood be lies on couches.
One Mother rests: another feeds the Infant. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

Der gemeinsame K├╢nig, auf viele Stellen verteilt, ruht in den ruhenden M├╝ttern sich selbst ├╝berlassen in jedem Holze. Eine andere tr├дgt das Kalb die Mutter sitzt ruhig. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Derselbe K├╢nig, viel umhergetragen, liegt auf den Lagern sorglos in den H├╢lzern, Die eine n├дhrt das Kalb, die Mutter schlummert; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕реБ рдЬреАрд░реНрдгрд╛рд╕реНрд╡реЛрд╖рдзреАрд╖реБ рдЖрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреН рдЖрд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдкрд░рд╛рдГ рдирд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдЕрдиреВрд░реБрддреН рдЕрдиреБрд░реБрдиреНрдзрдиреН рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреБрдЧреБрдгреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рдиреБрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрдирдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рджреНрдпреЛ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╕реБ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореБрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирд╛рд╕реБ рддрд░реБрдгреАрд╖реБ рдкрд▓реНрд▓рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд╕реНрд╡реЛрдкрдзреАрд╖реБ рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рддрд╛ рдУрд╖рдзрдпрдГ рдЕрдкреНрд░рд╡реАрддрд╛рдГ рдХреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рдирд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрд░реЗрддрд╕реНрдХрд╛рдГ рдЕрдирднреНрдпрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдирд╛ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╡рддреНрдпреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрд╡рддреЗ рдлрд▓рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдкрдВ рдЪреЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрджрд┐рджрдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН рее рдЖрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреН ред тАШрдХреНрд╖рд┐ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдЧрддреНрдпреЛрдГ’ ред рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рдЕрдиреВрд░реБрддреН ред тАШ рдЕрдиреЛ рд░реБрдз рдХрд╛рдореЗ ’ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдордкрд┐ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГред рддрд░реБрдгреАрд╖реБ ред’ рдирдЮреНрд╕реНрдирдЮреАрдХрдХреНрдЦреНрдпреБрдВрд╕реНрддрд░рдгрддрд▓реБрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореБрдкрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдореН ’ ( рдкрд╛. рдо. рек.рез:резрел.рем ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдбреАрдкреН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдГред тАШ рдЭрдпрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреБрдкреЛ рд╡рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╕реБрд╡рддреЗ ред тАШ рд╖реВрдЩреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдЧрд░реНрднрд╡рд┐рдореЛрдЪрдиреЗ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓рдЯрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдГ рее рее реиреорее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬExisting in ancient plural nts, abiding afterwards in new, he enters into the young (herbs) as soon as they are produced; unimpregnated they become pregnant and bear fruit; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He is dwelling in the older (plants), growing up through the later ones, within the tender ones (even) when they are just born.
Having (him) within, (though) unimpregnated they give birth to (him). тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As is generally acknowledged, the feminine plurals in the first hemistich refer to plants; the idea is the common paradox that fire is covertly present in all plants because overt fire is produced from wood. Here the three types of plants must be 1) тАШolderтАЩ (p┼л╠Бrv─Б-) = woody and easily burned, 2) тАШlaterтАЩ (├бpar─Б-) = still green and obviously growing and fire grows up with them, 3) tender (t├бruс╣З─л-) = sprouting ones, which are hard to burn, but he’s in them already anyway. Most tr. take sady├бс╕е with Agni, not the new-born plants – e.g., Renou тАЬest d’un coup au dedans des (plantes) nouvelle(-ment) n├йesтАЭ – but sady├бс╕е is strongly associated with forms of тИЪjan, esp. in III (e.g., III.5.8 sady├│ j─Бt├бс╕е; sim. III.32.9, 10; 48.1), in the sense of тАЬjust born.тАЭ The covert presence of fire is the topic of the paradox in c: he is always within the plants (ant├бrvat─лс╕е) even though they have not been impregnated (├бprav─лt─Бс╕е) sexually.

+Griffith

Lodged in old plants, he grows again in younger, swiftly within the newly-born and tender.
Though they are unimpregned, he makes them fruitful. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

In den fr├╝heren hausend, in die sp├дteren nachwachsend ist er sogleich in den neugeborenen jungen Pflanzen. Die Schwangeren geb├дren ihn unbelegt. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

In fr├╝hern ruhend w├дchst er nach in sp├дtern, in den so eben nur gebornen Jungfrau’n; Ob unbelegt, geb├дren doch die schwangern; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe child of two mothers sleeps in the west, but (in the morning) the single infant proceeds unobstructed (through the sky); these are the functions of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mitra and Varuс╣Зa: Mitra presiding over day; Varuс╣Зa over the night, both being forms of one Agni

+Jamison Brereton

He who was lying down far awayтАФnow he who has two mothers roams without a binding (rope), their only calf.
These are the commandments of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa: Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

There seems to be a consensus that the phrase ┼Ыay├║с╕е par├бst─Бt in p─Бda a refers to a form of Agni in the other world, that is, to the sun in some manifestation (see esp. Geldner n. 6ab). This seems to me entirely unnecessary and a cosmic intrusion in a sustained description that is otherwise entirely focused on the ritual fire (vss. 1-9).

Instead the hemistich seems to contrast the fire that was immanent and motionless (┼Ыay├║с╕е) in the plants, as described in vs. 5, released after birth and roaming restlessly, as a newly kindled fire does. The depiction of his resting place as тАШfar awayтАЩ (par├бst─Бt) may seem exaggerated if only plants are involved, but conceptually, and to a certain extent physically (since the kindling wood has to have been gathered from somewhere), it seems to me appropriate.

+Griffith

Now lying far away, Child of two Mothers, he wanders unrestrained, the single youngling.
These are the laws of Varuna and Mitra. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Im Jenseits zur Ruhe gehend wandelt nunmehr das Zweim├╝tterkind als einsames unangebundenes Kalb. Dies ist das Walten des Mitra und Varuna. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Dort ferne ruhend, hier in Zweiten M├╝ttern, das eine Kalb, es wandert ungefesselt, Das sind des Mitra-Varuna Gesetze; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe child of two mothers, the invoker of the gods at sacrifices, the universal sovereign, proceeds thenceforward (in the sky); the root (of all), he abides (in the houses of the pious); the reciters of plural asant (words) offer him agreeable (praises); great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The one with two mothers is the Hotar, the sovereign king at the
rites. The top (of him) roams along (the logs), while his base rests
peacefully.
Those who speak delightful (speech) proffer delightful (things). тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b is a elaboration on and corrective of 6b. It is not the whole fire that wanders untethered, only the top of it (├бgram), while the base stays put on the hearth.

Most tr. take ├бgram as an acc. with ├бnu; I follow Renou (who in turn follows Bergaigne) in taking it as the neut. nom. subj.

The accent on c├бrati is contrastive with the immediately following kс╣г├йti, which opens a new clause.

+Griffith

Child of two Mothers, Priest, sole Lord in synods, he still precedes while resting as foundation.
They who speak sweetly bring him sweet addresses. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Das Zweim├╝tterkind ist der Hotri, bei dem Opfer der Allherr. Er bewegt sich nach der Spitze zu, der untere Teil bleibt ruhen. Unter erg├╢tzlichen Reden bringen sie erg├╢tzliche Opferspenden dar. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Sohn zweier M├╝tter, Priester, Herr der Feste, nach aufw├дrts geht er, ruhend ist die Wurzel; Ihm bringen liebes dar, die lieblich reden; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll (creatures) approaching too near his confines are beheld with their faces turned away as (an enemy) flies from a combatant; obvious (to all), he penetrates the water for its destruction; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

His every approach appears right in your face, like that of a champion battling up close.
The thought acts as go-between to the tribute of the cow [=ghee as
oblation]. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse contains quite oblique phraseology. The first half-verse appears to describe the increasingly aggressive ritual fire after it has been kindled. I take ─Бy├бt as the neut. pres. part. to тИЪi + ─Б╠БтАШcomeтАЩ, substantivized to mean тАШapproach, adventтАЩ, and I supply a gen. тАШof himтАЩ, which is parallel to the gen. simile in p─Бda a. The growing fire is compared to a fighter involved in close combat. I have rendered prat─лc─л╠Бnam, lit. тАШturned outward, opposite, face to faceтАЩ, as the slangy тАШright in your faceтАЩ to convey the belligerent nearness of the fireтАЩs approach.

The c p─Бda is likewise hard to interpret. As Geldner notes, the lexeme ant├бr тИЪcar is generally used for the journey between earth and heaven undertaken by Agni, the messenger or тАЬgo-betweenтАЭ for the earthly and heavenly realms. This usage is found in fact in the very next vs., 9b, where Agni is clearly the subject and is journeying through the space between heaven and earth – as well as in numerous other passages (see esp. X.4.2). As Geldner also points out, in I.173.3 it is тАШSpeechтАЩ (v─Б╠Бk) who plays this role. Similarly, in our passage тАШthoughtтАЩ (mat├н-) – i.e., as often, thought that has taken shape as ritual speech – is the subject and undertakes the role of messenger. As for the tribute of the cow (niс╣гс╣г├нdhaс╣Г g├│с╕е), with Geldner I take this as referring to the bovine product that serves as oblation, namely ghee. Thus, ritual speech makes the swift journey to the gods in heaven from the ritual ground, bringing the news of the oblation or serving as its envoy. On niс╣гс╣г├нdh- see comm. ad III.51.5.

+Griffith

As to a friendly warrior when he battles, each thing that comes anear is seen to meet him.
The hymn commingles with the cow’s oblation. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIn those (plural nts) the aged messenger (of the gods) constantly abides; mighty, he presses with the radiant (sun) through the region of space; assuming various forms, he looks (complacently) upon us; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The gray messenger [=smoke] keeps bearing down on them
[=hearths? plants?]. The great one acts the go-between through the
luminous realm.
Bearing wondrous forms, he looks out upon us. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a the тАЬgray messengerтАЭ is Agni, gray because of his ash; I take the fem. pl. ─Бsu as referring to the plants (see vs. 5) that provide the fuel that feeds AgniтАЩs flames. The fire тАЬbears down on themтАЭ (/ тАЬkeeps pursuing themтАЭ; n├н veveti) as it spreads over the firewood. (A reference to his hearths is also possible, but I think less likely.) In contrast to the earthly spread of the fire depicted in p─Бda a, b shows it rising towards heaven in its messenger role. I take rocan├йna as an instr. of extent of space, rather than referring to AgniтАЩs own luminosity with the standard tr. However, taking it in the latter way would not appreciably alter the sense of the p─Бda.

The published translation is somewhat misleading, in having тАШbearingтАЩ for both n├н veveti in a and b├нbhrat in c, though of course English тАШbearтАЩ has entirely different senses in the two idioms.

Deep within these the hoary envoy pierceth; mighty, he goeth to the realm of splendour,
And looketh on us, clad in wondrous beauty. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬPervading and protecting (all), possessing grateful and immortal radiance, he preserves the supreme path (or the rains), for Agni knows all these worlds; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Viс╣гс╣Зu, the cow-protector, protects the highest pen, establishing his own dear, immortal domains.
Agni knows all these worlds. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse continues the theme of vss. 8-9, AgniтАЩs role as go-between. Its point is to show us that Agni as messenger reaches to the highest places in heaven, those defined by the endpoint of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs famous striding. But the introduction of Viс╣гс╣Зu also initiates the transition from the exclusive focus on Agni and his kindling.

Note the alliteration: (go)p─Б╠Бс╕е paramaс╣Г p─Бti p─Б╠Бthaс╕е, priy─Б╠БтАж

+Griffith

Visnu, the guardian, keeps the loftiest station, upholding dear, immortal dwelling-places.
Agni knows well all these created beings. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe twin pair (day and night) adopt various forms; one of them shines brightly, the other is black; twin sisters are they, one black and the other white; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The twins [=Night and Dawn] have assumed wondrous forms, each one for herself. One of them shines; the other is black;
the dusky one and the ruddy one are sisters. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The y├бd in p─Бda c has no obvious function. JSK (I.136) interprets the p─Бda as containing an тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction (тАЬthe dusky one and [the one] who is ruddyтАЭ), with y├бd instead of y─Б╠Бby attraction to the any├бd of b. Although this is a tempting way to account for the y├бd, in addition to the wrong gender the rel. is wrongly positioned: we should expect *y├бd/y─Б╠Бca ├бruс╣г─л. GeldnerтАЩs suggestion, that this contains the izafe-like [not GeldnerтАЩs term] y├бd that attaches appositives in Vedic prose, may be correct. ItтАЩs also worth noting that the structure of c is identical to 12a m─Бt─Б╠Б ca y├бtra duhit─Б╠Бca dhen┼л╠Б, with two nom. singulars conjoined by double ca, a yasubordinator between them, and a dual nom. at the end of the p─Бda referring jointly to the two singulars. So it is possible that the y├бd of 11c comes from the model of 12a, where y├бtra has function.

Ye, variant Pair, have made yourselves twin beauties: one of the Twain is dark, bright shines the other;
And yet these two, the dark, the red, are Sisters. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhere the mother and daughter, two productive kine, unite, they nourish each other; I worship them both in (the firmament), the dwelling of the waters great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They nourish each other: earth and heaven by the interchange of moisture

+Jamison Brereton

Where the mother and the daughter [also =Night and Dawn], the two sap-yielding milk-cows, give suck jointly,
I reverently invoke the two within the seat of truth. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner I interpret this fem. pairing to be Night and Dawn, who in the previous vs. were identified as sisters. They jointly nurse the infant fire at the early morning sacrifice; the reference is probably to twilight, the transition between Night and Dawn. Renou prefers to identify them as Heaven and Earth, but this requires him to interpret Heaven as a female, and it also makes less ritual sense. On the other hand, the same fem. dual sam─лc─л╠Бis used in vs. 12 of Heaven and Earth.

+Griffith

Where the two Cows, the Mother and the Daughter, meet and give suck yielding their lordly nectar,
I praise them at the seat of law eternal. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Wo die beiden immermelken K├╝he, Mutter und Tochter, gemeinsam das Kalb s├дugen, rufe ich die beiden am Sitze der Wahrheit an. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Wo beide K├╝he, Mutter und die Tochter, vereinigt s├дugen, reichen Nektar str├╢mend; Sie beide preis’ ich in dem heil’gen Sitze; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLicking the calf of the other, one of them lows aloud; the cow offers her udder for the one that is without mosture (the earth), and she (the earth) is refreshed by the milk of the rain; great and unequalles is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Licking the calf: the calf is said to be Agni, the cow with milk is the sky, whose udder is the cloud, whence the rain of which the earth is in want descends: с╣Ыtasya s─Б prayas─Б pinvateс╕╖─Б = jalavarjit─Б pс╣Ыthivy ─Бdityasyodakena sikt─Б bhavati varс╣г─Бk─Бle (─Бdity─Бjjayte vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нiс╕е–Manu 3.76), the earth without water is sprinkled by the water of the sun in the rainy season

+Jamison Brereton

Licking the calf [=Agni] of another [=firestick/Night], she [=oblation/ Dawn] lows: in what form has the milk-cow deposited her udder?
Iс╕Н─Б [/Refreshment] has swelled with the milk of truth. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The p─Бda-initial position of any├бsy─Б(с╕е) strongly suggests that it is indefinite (тАШanotherтАЩ, not тАШthe otherтАЩ), contra the standard tr. Since definite any├б- тАж any├б- (тАЬthe one тАж the otherтАЭ) is correctly positioned in 11b, 15b, and 17ab, I think we should take the contrastive positioning seriously and connect this phraseology with 4c, which also contains initial any├б- (any─Б╠Бvats├бm bh├бrati kс╣г├йti m─Бt─Б╠БтАЬAnother bears the calf; the mother rests peacefully.тАЭ). In that passage the тАЬmotherтАЭ of the fire, the lower kindling stick, rested, while the upper kindling stick, identified as тАЬanother,тАЭ carried the infant fire. Here the situation is reversed: the any─Б╠Б- form refers to the mother of the calf/fire, which is now being licked by a different feminine entity – in this case, in my opinion, the ghee oblation. A second pairing also imposes itself, however: in vs. 12 we had a different feminine duo: Night and Dawn. Their proximity in 12 invites an alternative reading of 13a, underscoring the temporal transition, with Night functioning as the mother of the fire, but Dawn taking over, tending it and bellowing over it. This latter interpr. seems to be continued in the next vs. (14ab).

I confess that I do not entirely understand the purport of p─Бda b (nor, as far as I can see, does anyone else). The hemistich is found identically also in X.27.14cd, though given the virtual impenetrability of that hymn, this doesnтАЩt help much. Contra Geldner (/Grassmann, etc.), I do not think bh┼л╠Б- here is тАШworldтАЩ, nor that the instr. expression k├бy─Б bhuv─Б╠Бmeans тАЬin welcher WeltтАЭ (see Oldenberg for objection to this tr.). Instead I take bh┼л╠Б- as тАШformтАЩ or (with Oldenberg, etc.) тАШexistence-formтАЩ, with the phrase meaning тАЬin what shape or guise.тАЭ I suspect that the p─Бda asks how the surrogate mother/cow, who took over from the fireтАЩs mother in p─Бda a, will deliver nourishment (symbolized by her udder) to the infant fire. The answer may be given in p─Бda c: it is тАЬthe milk of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya тАж p├бyas-), which we might further translate into тАЬthe milk of correct ritual speech.тАЭ

+Griffith

Loud hath she lowed, licking the other’s youngling. On what world hath the Milch-cow laid her udder?
This Ila streameth with the milk of Order. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Das Kalb der anderen leckend br├╝llte sie. In welcher Welt hat die Kuh ihr Euter verborgen? Die Ila schwoll von Milch der Wahrheit. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Das Kalb der andern leckend br├╝llte laut sie; in welcher Welt legt hin die Kuh ihr Euter? Sie schwillt vom Trunk und von der Milch des Opfers; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe earth wears bodies of many forms; she abides on high cherishing her year and a half old (calf); knowing the abode of the truth (the sun), I offer worship; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The earth: padya in the text is explained as bh┼лmi, deriving it from pad, or foot, the earth, i.e. having been created from the feet of the Creator; abides on high: on the altar; year and a half old calf: tryavim sardh─Б saс╣Гvatsara vayasko vatsaс╕е, a calf a year and half old; i.e, the sun of that period, or it may apply to the sun, as the protector (aviс╕е) of the three (tri) worlds; the abode of truth: с╣Ыtasya sadman, satyabh┼лtasy─Бdityasya sth─Бnam, the plural ce of the sun, who is one with the truth

+Jamison Brereton

At her feet she of many shapes [=Dawn] clothes herself in wondrous forms. She stands erect, constantly licking the (calf) three
lambing-seasons old.
I roam through the seat of truth as a knowing one. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes p├бdy─Б as merely a locational тАШuntenтАЩ, contrasting with ┼лrdhv─Б╠Бat the beginning of the next p─Бda. It seems unlikely that a formation with so much lexical content would be used in so colorless a manner, esp. given the deployment of pad├б-forms elsewhere in the hymn (pad├й iva n├нhite beginning the next vs. [15a], pad├й g├│с╕е 1b, padajс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е 2b). The тАЬfeetтАЭ of Dawn are presumably, in naturalistic terms, the light of dawn nearest to the horizon; shining through morning mists it will take on various shapes and colors. (L├╝ders [617 n. 3] suggests that the various shapes and forms are vegetation on the earth, which is also worth considering.) But in mytho-ritual terms, if Dawn is the cow nurturing the young fire in 13b (as well as p─Бda b in this vs.), the тАЬwondrous formsтАЭ (v├бp┼лс╣Гс╣гi) she clothes herself in and the тАЬmany shapesтАЭ she possesses (purur┼л╠Бp─Б) are the forms and colors of the fire over which she stands. That the scene is set on the ritual ground is suggested by p─Бda c, where тАЬIтАЭ roam across тАЬthe seat of truthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бsya s├бdma), which I take as a reference to seat of the ritual. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), however, interpret the p─Бda as simply meaning тАЬI wander тАШim GeisteтАЩтАЭ – I think because of the vidv─Б╠Бn тАШknowingтАЩ, though that word usually refers to knowledge of the ritual or to cosmic knowledge related to the religio-ritual system. With Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) I take purur┼л╠Бp─Б as fem. nom. sg.; however, it can equally be neut. acc. pl. (with Grassmann and Renou) modifying v├бp┼лс╣Гс╣гi. The choice actually has almost no effect on the sense of the p─Бda.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLike two (distinguishing) impressions, they (day and night) are plural ced visible in the midst (between heaven and earth), one hidden, one manifest; the path (of both) is common, and that is universal (for good and evil) great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Like two footprints set down within the wondrous one [=Agni? ritual ground?], the one of the two is hidden, the other visible [=Night
and Dawn].
Their pathway has a single goal, (but goes) separately. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems to continue the theme of Night and Dawn. The any├бd тАж any├бd construction of p─Бda b echoes that in 11b, where Night and Dawn were first introduced, and in fact our p─Бda b, with one hidden and one visible, paraphrases 11b, with one shining and the other black, and forms a small ring.

Moreover, the two тАЬset down within the wondrous oneтАЭ echoes 12c с╣Ыt├бsya t├й s├бdasy ─лс╕╖e ant├бс╕е тАЬI reverently invoke the two within the seat of truth.тАЭ I take dasm├бto refer to the ritual fire/ritual ground, and one of the marvels is that two such large entities (Night and Dawn) can fit into something so small.

The vs. also recycles various thematically significant lexical items: pad├б- (see comm. ad 14); nihit├й echoing n├н dadhe (13b); ant├бr (12c and passim: 2c, 5b, 5c, 8c, 9b, 12c; ant├бr is in a sense the signature word of this hymn); any├бd тАж any├бd 11b.

The тАШpathwayтАЩ (pathy─Б╠А) takes us back to III.54.5 where a question about тАЬthe pathway leading to the godsтАЭ (dev─Б╠Бm╠Р├бch─Б pathy─Б╠А) initiated the mysteries that have dogged us ever since.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the kine without their young, abiding (in the heaven), and though unmilked, yet yielding milk and ever fresh and youthfu,l be shaken (so as to perform their functions); great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The kind: either the regions of space of the clouds

+Jamison Brereton

Let the milk-cows [=Dawns? plants crackling as they burn?] be noisy, those which are without young (yet) sap-yielding, unfailing, not
milked out,
becoming young ever anew. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The miraculous milkers in this vs. are taken by all standard tr. as rain clouds, flg. one of S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs suggestions (the other being the heavenly regions). In context this interpr. seems perverse. The verse forms part of a tight little section (beginning with vs. 11) concerning Night and Dawn and their nourishing of the infant ritual fire. Our vs. esp. echoes vs. 12: dhen├бvaс╕е тАж sabard├║gh─Бс╕е тАж ├бpradugdh─Бс╕е тАЬmilk-cows, sap-yielding, not milked outтАЭ is the equivalent in the plural of 12ab dhen┼л╠Б, sabard├║ghe dh─Бpayete тАЬthe two milk-cows, sap-yielding, give suckтАЭ in the dual. I find it highly unlikely that the vocabulary here repeated from 12 would refer to entirely different entities (clouds), which, moreover, have no connection with the dawn ritual depicted here. Instead, in the course of this section the joint nurturing activity of Night and Dawn (11-12) has given way to the dominance of Dawn over Night (13ab, 14ab), and though both Night and Dawn are present in vs. 15, one of them (Night) is hidden (15b). This trend accords with the natural phenomenon: at dawn, light dissipates darkness. In our vs. 16 the plural cows either represent the Dawns in general – the plural of Dawn being often interchangeable with the singular – or the beams of light, the тАЬdawn cows,тАЭ of a single Dawn. The expression тАЬbecoming new ever againтАЭ (p─Бda c n├бvy─Б-navy─Б yuvat├бyo bh├бvant─лс╕е) might favor the former possibility, since it reminds us of the daily parade of ever-new youthful Dawns. My identification of the cows with the dawns here admittedly leaves the noisiness (тАЬlet them be noisy,тАЭ ─Б╠БтАж dhunayant─Бm) unexplained. I would suggest either that there is also a reference to the crackling of the fire wood as the ritual fire is kindled at dawn, or that it refers to the general noise attendant on dawn as the various creatures awake, including real cows mooing to be milked. Note that already in vs. 13a Dawn (in my interpr.) тАШlowsтАЩ (mim─Бya) over the infant fire. I think we can safely banish the putative rain clouds.

+Griffith

Let the milch-kine that have no calves storm downward, yielding rich nectar, streaming, unexhausted,
These who are ever new and fresh and youthful. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Es sollen heranrauschen die Milchk├╝he, die kein Junges haben und doch immer melk sind, die ergiebigen, nicht vorgemolkenen, immer wieder aufs neue sich verj├╝ngend. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

Die K├╝he, frei des Kalbes, m├╢gen rauschen, neumilchend, ungemolken, immerstr├╢mend, Die jugendlichen, fort und fort erneuten, gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the showerer roars in other (regions) he sends down the rain upon a different herd, for he is the victor, the auspicious, the sovereign; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Upon a different herd: anyasmin y┼лthe, a herd, or troop,of regions, di┼Ы─Бm vс╣Ыnde

+Jamison Brereton

Though the bull goes about roaring within the one (herd of) cows, he deposits his seed in the other herd.
For he is the earth-protector; he is the apportioner; he is king. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction. I consider this vs. to be transitional between the fire-kindling vss. and the arrival of Indra at the sacrifice. I therefore think that the reference is ambiguous. In the published introduction. I suggested a trio of possible referents: Agni, Soma, and Indra. I now think it is only Agni and Indra and that Agni is the sole referent in ab, with transition from Agni to Indra in c.

This opinion is very different from the standard, which takes Parjanya as the subject here (flg. on the supposed rain cloud vs.). The issue is further complicated by the fact that in the next hymn (III.56.3) yet another being, possibly Tvaс╣гс╣нar or Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs son, is described as retodh─Б╠Бvс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е тАЬa bull, depositor of semen,тАЭ which matches our vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е тАж n├н dadh─Бti r├йtaс╕е. Although I must concede that Parjanya is described with the same phrase as III.56.3 in VII.101.6 and is said to deposit semen also in V.83.1, such designations are not exclusive to Parjanya. In I.128.3 it is Agni who is тАж r├йto vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бс╕е k├бnikradad, d├бdhad r├йtaс╕е k├бnikradat тАЬa bull ever-roaring, depositing his semenтАЩ (with тИЪkrand, rather than тИЪru, тАШroarтАЩ), and I think Agni is the referent here as well. I do not entirely understand the two herds of cows, but suggest that it may have to do with the embryonic doctrine of the cycle of waters that is later developed in the Upaniс╣гads, whereby rain falls from heaven and causes plants to grow; the plants, as fuel, produce/give birth to the fire, whose smoke goes to heaven and becomes clouds from which the rain falls, and the cycle begins again. Our passage may have an abbreviated form of this: the bull Agni is roaring (that is, crackling as fire) among one set of cows (plants as firewood); the smoke goes to heaven and the rain (his semen) falls to earth and produces plants (the other herd).

Note vs. 5 much earlier in the hymn, where it is said of the plants тАЬHaving (him) within, (though) unimpregnated they give birth to (him).тАЭ The transition from Agni to Indra occurs in p─Бda c, in my interpr. Both Agni and Indra can be called kс╣г├бp─Бvant- (/kс╣гap─Б╠Бvant-) тАШearth-protectorтАЩ, indeed simultaneously. (See X.29.1 and my тАЬ┼Ъleс╣гa in the Rig Veda?тАЭ [Fs. Gerow], 163-64.) Indeed this epithet is even more flexible: as I discussed in the Gerow Fs., the first element may be either kс╣г├б(m) тАШearthтАЩ or kс╣г├бp- тАШnightтАЩ. (For the possible morphological analyses, see the loc. cit.) Under the latter analysis, the epithet would be appropriate only for Agni, but under the former to both Agni and Indra, so the first word in c may slip from clear reference to Agni to double reference. The following two words, bh├бga- and r─Б╠Бjan-, are also used in the RV of both Agni and Indra, though тАШkingтАЩ is more common for Indra than Agni. The transition is complete.

+Griffith

What time the Bull bellows in other regions, another herd receives the genial moisture;
For he is Bhaga, King, the earth’s Protector. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Wenn der Stier unter anderen K├╝hen br├╝llt, legt er in die andere Herde seinen Samen, denn er ist der Herrscher, er der Bhaga, er der K├╢nig. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Wenn br├╝nstig br├╝llt der Stier nach andern K├╝hen, so setzt in andre K├╝he er den Samen; Er ist ja F├╝rst, Vertheiler, Erdbesch├╝tzer; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe proclaim, people, the wealth of the hero, (Indra), in horses; the gods know his (affluence); six, or five and five, harnessed to his car, convey him; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Six or five: с╣гoс╕╖h─Б yukt─Бс╕е pa├▒capa├▒ca vahanti = either the six seasons of the year, or, by combining the cold and dewy seasons, five; these are figurately Indra’s horses.

+Jamison Brereton

The heroтАЩs abundance of horses we will proclaim just now, o people. The gods know of it.
Yoked sixfold, five after five they convey (Indra) hither. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In my interpr. this vs. announces the arrival of Indra with a splendid team of horses. This new topic is signaled by pr├б n├║ voc─Бma beginning p─Бda b. The exact arrangement of the six and five isnтАЩt clear to me. Renou suggests that the double n├║ indicates that there are two separate clauses here. He may be right (тАЬnow there is an abundance of horses of the hero; we will proclaim (it) nowтАЭ), though the difference in sense is slight.

+Griffith

Let us declare the Hero’s wealth in horses, O all ye folk: of this the Gods have knowledge.
Sixfold they bear him, or by fives are harnessed. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Jetzt wollen wir des Helden sch├╢nes Rossegespann verk├╝nden, ihr Leute; die G├╢tter kennen es. Je f├╝nf und f├╝nf in sechs Reihen geschirrt fahren sie ihn her. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

Lasst preisen nun den Rossbesitz des Helden, ihr Menschen, uns; es kennen ihn die G├╢tter; Ihn fahren sechzig, angeschirrt zu f├╝nfen; gross ist allein der G├╢tter Geistesf├╝lle.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe divine Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б the impeller (of all), the multiform, has begotten and nourished a numerous progeny, for all these worlds are of him; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

God Tvaс╣гс╣нar, the impeller providing all forms, flourishes; he has begotten offspring in great quantity,
and all these creatures here are his. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is striking that p─Бda a is reused in the famous Yama-Yam─л dialogue hymn (X.10.5b), where Yam─л claims that Tvaс╣гс╣нar made them a married couple in the womb. I do not think there is an echo of that story here; the point of intersection is simply the association of Tvaс╣гс╣нar with conception, pregnancy, and birth (cf., e.g., X.184).

Acdg. to the standard interpr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], Renou; cf. Klein DGRV I.218, K├╝mmel 314), praj─Б╠Бс╕е is to be construed with pup├│с╣гa, on the basis of X.170.1 praj─Б╠Бс╕е pupoс╣гa purudh─Б╠БтАж This is not impossible, but it seems unnecessary, esp. as the latter hymn is quite late. It also implies that purudh─Б╠Бshould also be construed with pup├│с╣гa, but this is impossible because jaj─Бna is unaccented. It is also unlikely that praj─Б╠Бс╕е and purudh─Б╠Бshould be separated, given purudh─Б╠Бpraj─Б╠Бv─Бn in the next hymn (III.56.3b).

At best we can take praj─Б╠Бс╕е purudh─Б╠Бwith both verbs: тАЬthrives with regard to offspring in great quantity and has begotten them [=offspring in great quantity]тАЭ or perhaps тАЬthrives with regard to offspring and has begotten them [=offspring] in great quantity.тАЭ Such an interpr., with an acc. of respect and a fundamentally intransitive verb, follows that of K├╝mmel (314). I do not believe that pup├│с╣гa here can have the transitive/causative sense that the other tr. ascribe to it (e.g., Renou тАЬa fait fleurir les cr├йaturesтАЭ).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe has filled the two vast receptacles (heaven and earth) united (with creatures); they are both penetrated by his lustre; the hero spoiling the treasures (of the foe) is renowned; great and unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The two vast receptacles: camvau, the two vessels in which gods and men and men eat, camanty adanty anayor devamanuс╣гaс╕е; this would imply vessels or ladles, but the explanation is that the two that are or enjoyed by living beings, i.e. heaven and earth

+Jamison Brereton

He [=Indra?] has raised up together the two great bowls (to be) united. Both of them are crammed with his goods.
The hero is famed for finding goods. тАУ Great is the one and only
lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I assume that the subject of this vs. is Indra. One of his standard cosmogonic deeds involves the creation and separation of the two worlds, the separation here implied by the material crammed between them. Indra is of course commonly identified as a v─лr├б-; he also тАЬfinds goodsтАЭ (e.g., II.13.11, VIII.61.5), though so do other gods as well as mortals.

+Griffith

The two great meeting Bowls hath he united: each of the Pair is laden with histreasure.
The Hero is renowned for gathering riches. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬOur king, the nourisher of all, abides (in the firmament) nearest to this earthlike a benevolent friend; the valiant (Maruts) precede him (when abroad), and dwell in his mansion; great and unequalles is the might of the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

And he who suckles all of us [=Agni] dwells peacefully on this earth here, like a king with established alliances,
stationed in front like heroes stationed for protection. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first three p─Бdas here are almost identical to I.73.3abc, where Agni is definitely the referent. For disc. of some of the detail, see comm. there.

+Griffith

Yea, and on this our earth the All-Sustainer dwells like a King with noble friends about him.
In his protection heroes rest in safety. Great is the Cods’ supreme and sole dominion.

+Geldner

Und diese unsere Erde bewohnt der Alln├дhrende wie ein K├╢nig, der gute Freunde hat, Wacht haltend wie die in Deckung liegenden M├дnner. -Gro├Я ist die einzige Asuramacht der G├╢tter.

+Grassmann

тАЬThe plural nts, Indra, come to perfection by you; from you the waters (flow); earth bears her treasures for you; may we, your friends, be sharers of these blessings; great unequalled is the might of the gods.тАЭ

The plants and the waters offer tribute to you; the earth bears wealth for you, Indra.
May we be your comrades, sharing in the valuables. тАУ Great is the one and only lordship of the gods.

Rich in their gifts for thee are herbs and waters, and earth brings all her wealth for thee, O Indra.
May we as friends of thine share goodly treasures. Great is the Gods’ supreme and sole dominion.
